When she throws on her robe and pads through the hallway, she finds a soft, warm toned glow emitting from her living room as she nears the end. Among the music, there is the soft clatter of what could only be Rio messing with something in the kitchen. She finds a fire lit in her fireplace with their stockings hung just above them, items nearly busting out of the seams. Agatha smiles as she remembers them hanging them up together just a few hours prior. 

She’d never been much into the holiday spirit, so her holiday decorations were few and far between, but it had only taken a moment for Rio to convince her that they needed to make a store trip to rectify that.

So now, in addition to the stockings, there’s a new found four foot tree—it was the only size on the shelf at such late notice— stuffed away in the corner of her apartment, just by the windows and it’s got twinkling lights haphazardly thrown in between the branches and a can of fake snow sprayed into it. There’s mistletoe dangling under all her door frames and obnoxiously big candle sticks place on all of her shelves along with little trinkets of elves and reindeer. But best of all, there's the smell of cinnamon in the air mixing with the all too familiar smell of roasting coffee beans and suddenly her apartment feels a lot like a home.

When Agatha approaches her kitchen she finds Rio in an apron, hair thrown back into a festive claw clip with little elves on it and a piping bag in her hand as she concentrates on layering what appears to be Cinnamon rolls with icing. Between the tinge of frosting on her cheek and the way her tongue is trapped between her teeth in concentration, it’s a toss up at which is cuter. 

“And what do you think you’re doing,” Agatha asks with a teasing lilt, her arms crossed in mock disapproval as she leans against the side of the kitchen door frame. 

Rio looks up to her in surprise. “Oh, you’re up!”

And then she smiles and Agatha’s breath catches at the sight. She finds herself just standing there like a love struck idiot, drinking in the sight of this woman as if it were her last drop of water in the desert.

“I’m making cinnamon rolls,” Rio comments as she goes back to layering the icing over the pastry. “It was a tradition for Christmas in my house growing up and it’s just one of those things I’ve always held onto. I normally just buy the Pilsbury can from the store, but I wanted to try something new.”

Agatha takes that Rio has homemade these by the plethora of ingredients strode across her kitchen island, but even with the giant mess, she’s never been so enamored in her life. She slowly stalks up to Rio’s side and looks down over her girlfriend’s creation. Surprisingly, they look very good.

“They look amazing, love,” Agatha comments as she leans down and places a kiss to the top of Rio’s head. “They smell really good too. This is your first time making them, you say?”

Rio nods. “Mhmm, I’ve baked before but it’s only been cookies, croissants and a few loaves of focaccia.”

Agatha raises a brow. “So you’ve been holding out on me this whole time?”

Rio laughs. “I said I’ve baked before, not that it was any good.”

“But was it,” Agatha asks curiously.

Rio turns to look up at her, a beaming smile on her face as she winks, “Of course.”

Agatha shoves her lightly with a laugh as she takes a finger and dips it into the icing on top of the rolls, she pulls it to her lips and sucks it into her mouth to taste. She hums in contentment. “That’s actually really good.”

Rio chuckles. “Yeah, that’s actually store bought.”

Agatha gasps. “Cheater!”

“It’s a compromise, baby,” Rio defends. “You either get homemade cinnamon rolls or homemade icing. I have not got the time to go all out here. We’ve got presents to open! There is Christmas cheer to be had!”

Agatha rolls her eyes, but there’s a fond smile on her lips. “The cinnamon rolls better be good then.”

“Oh they will be. Trust.”

Rio wasn’t lying about her baking being good. All the knowledge she lacks in cooking she makes up for in pastries. The cinnamon rolls are flaky and sweet and absolutely divine. It takes Rio a full twenty minutes to be convinced Agatha isn’t lying to her, but when she finally relents and lets herself be complimented, Agatha can see a monster brewing. Rio is never going to live this down.

Christmas for Agatha growing up was less about the presents and more about making sure to thank her lord and savior, Jesus Christ. There was an evening church service on Christmas Eve and then they would have their church family back at her mom’s brownstone in Brooklyn and then on Christmas morning they had another church service before their family came over for lunch. Which mostly just consisted of her mother, grandmother, and a few cousins, aunts, and uncles she’d never cared to get to know. She was lucky if she got a plate of food, let alone a present. Something about ‘the undeserving eat last’ and that gave room for her gluttonous cousins to wipe the platters clean. 

So as it turns out, she was wildly underprepared to spend Christmas morning with someone like Rio who had only known leaving cookies out for Santa and sprinkling reindeer food in the yard with her siblings the night before and then waking up at six am, running down the stairs to open presents. Her parents would shuffle in some time later, mom retreating to the stove to start the cinnamon rolls and her dad would ravage the living room with a trash bag to pick up all the leftover wrapping paper. 

They open the presents under the tree that have been itching at Rio ever since she’d seen hers wrapped in a beautiful earthy green wrapping paper that definitely cost just a much, if not more, as the present they are covering where as Agatha gifts are wrapped in a glossy purple wrapping paper Rio had gotten at the store for .99 cents. Regardless, both papers get discarded across the living room, covering the ground in a green and purple collage and Agatha briefly thinks she could get used to this. Just instead of wrapping papers, pieces of them in a confined space together.

Rio opens her first present to find the Porsche 911 Lego set that she hugs and runs around the couch with for a laps, Agatha recording on her phone the entire time with a smile so bright she doesn’t even need to cut on the flash. When she tells Rio to stand still so she can take a picture, the younger woman holds the set out like a proud trophy before running back over to the tree and swapping her present for one of Agatha’s. She hands it to the other woman and admittedly, Agatha feels a little out of place. 

She tears back the purple wrapping paper with diligent fingers and tries not to look as awkward as she feels, but when she sees a framed photo of what appears to be some grainy security footage, she giggles. Her glasses were perched atop her head but she promptly tucks them back down in an effort to see. When she notices the subject of the photo, her breath hitches.

It’s them. 

It’s them on the dance floor of Rio’s workplace the night that everything changed. There’s bodies around them, but none stand out the way that Agatha and Rio are nearly one in the same. They’re pushed tightly together, smiles blistering as they dance to a tune only they could hear. 

“That’s the night I knew,” Rio starts, her eyes staring down at the photo. “I knew that I had somehow stumbled my way into one of the best things to ever happen to me.” With a shaky finger, she traces over the outlines of their bodies. “I never thought…”

Agatha isn’t an emotional crier by any means, but her eyes are welling up with tears despite it. The woman in the photo—that looks a lot like her—only had a taste of what she had found. She couldn’t have possibly known she’d been reliving the moment in the photo on Christmas morning on the floor of her apartment with the same woman. 

“First off, you did not stumble into this. You barged in,” Agatha laughs and makes a pointed effort to chase Rio’s full attention with her eyes until the younger woman turns to her and locks their gaze. As soon as she finds the tears in Rio’s eyes, she reaches out to cup her cheek and soothe the soft skin with the pad of her thumb. “Secondly, I’m so glad that you did.”

Rio’s smile is bright against the hand on her cheek as she leans into its hold, warming not only her face but Agatha’s heart as well. The moment stays still, neither one of them finding it necessary to break until the older woman finds herself wanting to deflect. “Don’t get me wrong, you were a pain in the ass.”

Rio snorts. “It worked didn’t it?”

“You’re so special Rio Vidal.”

“And don’t you forget it.” 

Sometime later, still surrounded by paper and boxes emptied of its contents, Agatha’s lounging out on the couch with a coffee in her hand, legs stretched in front of her and a hand playing with the back of Rio’s scalp as the younger girl sits at the coffee table, legs crossed underneath it while she puts together her lego set. 

It’s not the first thought that comes to her brain as she watches Rio building her car intently, but sometime during the process, she feels her heart begin to hurt as the imagine of Rio missing out on a Christmas morning like this for years—the emptiness she must’ve carried in her family's absence.

“Do you miss it,” Agatha asks softly. “Christmas with your family?”

It’s a brazen ask, but a necessary one to Agatha. She can see the tears glinting in Rio’s eyes upon resurfacing the memories and she’s grateful to get to know these broken parts of Rio so that she can start helping mend them back together.

When Rio doesn’t turn to her, but instead makes the coffee table in front of them the most important object in the room, Agatha knows her mistake and gears up for a subject change, but surprisingly, Rio offers a small smile. “Every day that I’m breathing.”

Agatha returns the soft smile, hoping Rio can feel the way her eyes are gleaming with love against the side of her face. “They didn’t deserve you, Rio.”

The younger woman nods softly. “I know.”

“What about your siblings? Do you hear from them,” Agatha shifts the conversation a bit and that’s when she notices Rio’s demeanor changes slightly, her shoulders getting taller and smile turning brighter.

“Yeah, actually, I hear from my brother a lot now. He was scared at first, still living with my parents and their opinions of me, but when they passed away he reached out to me and we kind of just catch up every now and again. He just moved out to Puerto Rico with a girlfriend. He seems happy,” she muses, fishing around her pocket for her phone before pulling up a picture of him smiling with a young woman, both of them matching flannel pajamas and Agatha gathers that Rio isn’t the only one big on traditions. “He sent this to me this morning.”

His smile is bright, eyes dark and milky just like Rio’s and Agatha suddenly finds herself yearning to meet a person she feels like she’s already met. 

“We should visit sometime,” Agatha comments to which the younger woman’s eyes widen, but so does her smile.

“You would do that,” Rio asks.

Agatha just shakes her head in disbelief. “Darling, when will you learn there isn’t much I wouldn’t do for you.”

The coffee that she’d been holding nearly splashes to their laps with the speed and velocity in which Rio leans over to kiss her. She tastes like cinnamon, coffee and a promising future. 

The week after Christmas leading up to New Years always feels like a fever dream. No one wants to work and Agatha’s productivity tracker shows it. She’d prepared for this just as she had in years past, but she hadn’t prepared to become one of those very people. Since spending Christmas with Rio and getting a taste of what the holiday season could really be about, she’s found herself taking advantage of the moments that she can get from behind her desk and allow herself to live instead of just existing. 

Lunch breaks are a little longer and she comes back from them actually feeling lighter. Not from the food, but instead her company. Five o’clock is the end of her workday. The long and unforgiving nights at the office are few and far between. She’s got somewhat of a grip on her life for the first time in years. Everything before was calculated with Harkness Enterprises in mind, now mostly everything is calculated in happiness. Gone are the times of doing things just for the sake of doing them. 

Which is how Rio convinces her that they really need to get out of the city for new years and find something different to do. The city would just become overrun with loud and smelly tourists—ever since Rio had found out people actually wear diapers to stand in Times Square she hasn’t let anyone go more than five minutes without a reminder. And well, Agatha isn’t one to deny Rio of anything so she lets herself be convinced in almost a matter of minutes. 

Agatha’s reply had been a sarcastic quip. “Is this where I find out you’re only with me for my money?” 

But she booked two nights in Italy anyway. Rio’s request of course. 

Rio shows up to Agatha’s apartment the night before they are due to leave with her duffle bag and a bright smile. She plops it to her side right as she enters and runs to make herself at home on the couch next to the older woman who has been typing away at an email up until that point. She sets her laptop to the side and pats her lap for Rio to take it’s place. When the younger woman straddles her legs, Agatha settles her hands on her waist.

“I’m so excited,” Rio whispers excitedly as she beams onto Agatha with her bright smile. She got her hands wrapped around Agatha’s neck, threading her fingers through her long hair and the older woman instantly puddles in her hands. “What time is our flight leaving?”

Agatha hums. “Whenever you’d like to go. I have Christian on standby to take us to the hangar. Everything’s prepped.”

Rio knits her brows. “You haven’t booked our flight?”

Agatha just chuckles. “No darling, we’re taking my private.”

“Oh, you’re kidding.”

And that’s how Rio and Agatha end up leaving that night. Rio had simply been too excited to see her private jet and who was Agatha to deny her of that joy? Again, she couldn’t deny her anything. It took a little time to finagle things around and add an extra night to their booking, but with it all said and done, Agatha finds herself contently closing her eyes in the backseat of her SUV, hand resting in Rio’s as Christian drives them to her hangar. 

When they arrived, she had planned to lead Rio to the proper area, but the woman took care of it all on her own as she all but threw herself out of the car and went barreling towards the inside of the hangar. There were a few jets in there—not Agatha’s as she shared the space with a few others—and they occupied Rio’s mind long enough for Agatha and Christian to get their bags from the trunk. 

Agatha approaches Rio some five minutes later as Christian takes to loading their luggage in the proper jet. Rio’s as quiet as Agatha has ever seen her as she ducks around the staggered planes across the expansive space. 

“Are all of these yours,” Rio asks curiously as she runs her hand along a parked black jet. It’s glossy and Agatha can see the way the younger woman is smiling in the reflection. 

“No,” Agatha answers simply with her arms folded across her chest. “These are just some other clients that store here as well. Mine is on the runway getting prepped for us.”

At that, Rio turns her head to follow where Agatha’s finger is pointing and her eyes light up at the sight of her jet being loaded with their luggage. It’s a small jet, but it’s the first Rio has ever seen in person and that much is clear by the way she’s bouncing on her toes. “I’m really excited now.”

The older woman laughs fondly, “Me as well. I haven’t seen the inside of it yet since I had the interior re-done a few months ago.”

Rio looks at her in disbelief, her cheeks tinging pink. “You’re so fucking rich and it’s so fucking hot.”

“You’re insane,” Agatha laughs, to which Rio just waves her off. It’s not a lie. Rio can definitely be described as insane, but the older woman is starting to release she’s not much better off. Especially when she’d chosen the interior with certain ulterior motives in mind. Motives she’s sure Rio would enjoy as well. “I am excited though. It's very expensive Italian leather. Scratch resistant, water proof…”

Agatha narrows her gaze at Rio with a visible, daring glint in her eye. “Extremely easy to clean if I may add.”

Agatha can tell Rio picks up on her intentions with the way she shifts her weight from one foot to the other and swallows visibly. She wants to raise an eyebrow, but doesn’t go for the obvious move and instead shuffles herself into Agatha's personal space and drops her voice to a breathy whisper. “You know, I still haven’t joined the mile high club.”

Agatha welcomes a smirk to her lips. Bullseye. “Now, that just simply won’t do. We’ll have to rectify that.”

As they step onto the jet, Agatha’s peacoat is the first article of clothing to hit the floor followed by the NYU hoodie Rio had been wearing. The captain of the jet had taken to getting a few things squared away in the hangar which left the two of them alone for just enough time to scratch a growing itch. Agatha’s backing Rio across the threshold of the jet, pushing the younger woman down into a seat before straddling her waist. Their lips are chapped and cold, but the way they're suddenly trying to devour each other whole fixes that in seconds. Rio’s got her hands tangled in Agatha’s hair, scratching against her scalp with purpose as the older woman takes to burrowing her hands in the skin around Rio’s waist. 

Agatha tries to keep their time limit close to the forefront of her mind but every time her hips grind down against Rio’s very hard midsection, she goes a little blank. Not to mention, the soft pants leaving her lover’s lips start to take precedence over listening for the footsteps of their captain. Clearly, she’s not the only one thinking the same because she can feel Rio reluctantly trying to pull her lips away only to be sucked back in seconds later as if the war she’s raging onto herself is too strong. Though, moments later she does regain some sense to put some space between them with a tug of Agatha’s hair and it does little to help the growing fire between her legs. 

When Rio speaks, her voice is scratchy and she has to clear the lump away, “Let’s put a pause on this before we traumatize the man who has to get us there safely, yeah?”

Agatha just nods, licking her lips and setting back onto Rio’s thighs. “He’s seen worse.”

There’s a low growl as Rio shows her distaste for Agatha and her previous escapades, but she nods in agreement anyways and brings her fingers up to wipe the wetness of salvia off of her lips. Agatha watches the entire action with darkened eyes. “After we’re in the air, I make no promises on what he might hear. You’re all mine”

“Baby,” Agatha whispers breathlessly before leaning forward to capture Rio’s lips again. It really was an involuntary reaction—the kiss. She can’t be blamed for the way Rio makes her body react. It’s just simply not fair. “It’s a long flight. We’ve got all the time in the world.” 

Rio’s eyes soften as she whispers between them. “All the time in the world is still not enough time with you.”

And then Agatha’s kissing her again, getting caught be damned. 

—

When they arrive in Italy, Rio’s nearly vibrating off the jet as Agatha sluggishly follows suit, her demeanor much more lagged down from their journey than her companion’s. She silently thanks god that she’d hired temporary assistants to unload their luggage in Christian’s absence because the thought of lifting anything makes her want to say fuck it and sleep on the plane for the remainder of their trip. 

Thankfully that doesn’t have to be an option and the damn near palace Agatha booked for the two of them is only a five minute ride away, so she’s only a few minutes away from a nice nap tucked into expensive sheets and an open window letting in the ocean’s breeze. 

However, Rio’s overly ready to explore so Agatha finds herself traipsing around the city on her last leg, but smiling the entire time because Rio is. They take enough pictures to last a lifetime and eat some of the best food they’ve ever had in their lives that Rio struggles to pronounce and Agatha giggles the entire time. 

When they get back to their place, it’s minutes before they’ve fallen into bed and their quiet snores mix with the sound of waves lapping against rocks. Agatha holds Rio tight like she might slip away in her sleep, but the first thing she feels when she wakes up is Rio’s nose pressing into the nape of her neck. She smiles warmly, pulling her even closer and settling into the sheets feeling excited for the new year for the first time in her life.

Later that night, they’ll stand on the balcony after giving the oven below a show and watch as the sun sets and the moon rises with champagne in their glasses and smiles creasing their sunburnt cheeks. They’ll kiss at midnight and kiss again a minute after and then a minute after that until there’s too many kisses to count. 

They’ll leave Italy and they’ll go back to lives that are on two completely different paths but manage to intertwine anyways. Agatha will feel Rio’s absence from her daily life harder than she could’ve ever imagined, but Rio sends her more texts, more memes and calls more than she could’ve ever seen herself being grateful for. They’ll meet up for lunch dates and actually digest their days because they aren’t one in the same any longer. 

Until they start spending most evenings and mornings together. Dinner dates with fancy dishes at fancy places, but still plenty of room for Shake Shack mixed in. Rio will finally learn what a Chablis is and Agatha will learn all about dipping your fries in a milkshake and complain the entire time just to hear Rio laugh. They’ll fall back into bed at Agatha’s apartment that will slowly gain the feeling of home she’d been chasing for years with the nightstand opposite her side of the bed containing the bunny eared booked Rio’s been reading, a fleet of half drunken water bottles and a picture of the two of them from some event. 

Her closet will become a space for two. A drawer in her wardrobe will contain Rio’s whimsical socks with characters from nearly every single animated movie Agatha thinks. Her vinyl collection will get played more than it ever has, the silence that once lingered so heavy will be impossible to hear any longer. 

They’ll slow dance in the living room and in the kitchen with the aroma of their dinner mixing between them. Agatha will go through dozens of aprons and Rio will be the one to end up wearing them. 

They’ll have dinner together time and time again, fall in love in a million different ways they could’ve never seen coming. They’ll spend holidays together both at home and abroad. Rio will gain so many stamps on her passport, but the one she’ll treasure the most is the stamp that marks her visit with her brother.

Agatha will meet him in the sweltering heat of Greece on a trip that neither of them saw coming, but when the invite had been extended, couldn’t say no to. Agatha will see Rio smile brighter and fuller than she has in a long time as she watches her brother say ‘I do’ to the love of his life and then she lets herself imagine what it would be like to finally be married to someone who loves her unconditionally.

She’ll think about it so much that she’ll buy a ring that’ll warm her pocket on nearly every single outing they go to together. There’s a few more weddings and a vacation or two before Agatha finally plans to get down on one knee. 

They’ll buy a brownstone home in Brooklyn together after touring so many Rio can’t remember one from another, but Agatha promises her that whichever they choose, they will design and repair until it’s absolutely perfect. So when they close on a home and open the front door to a new chapter of their lives, Agatha will get on one knee and Rio will burst into tears after joyfully screaming “what the fuck!”

They’ll laugh and they’ll fight more than they like to. They’ll argue over shower times and which corner the Christmas tree should go into. They’ll have many holiday gatherings, birthday parties and get togethers as they hold onto the friends that loved them separately before they were together. 

Agatha will get to wear an engagement ring she’s actually proud of that later adds a wedding band she can’t stop showing off no matter how many times Jen threatens to hide it from her. Rio will look on proudly, her own ring catching her eye and everything will just sort of start to make sense in life.  

She’ll save dozens of lives representing youth and Agatha will be her biggest cheerleader around every turn. Matt and her will open a firm and they’ll become some of the best known legal representatives in the city. Somehow, someway Agatha gets the life she’d always dreamed of and everything is in its right place despite her mothers constant warnings.

They’ll watch their circle grow and then dissipate. They’ll learn who truly loves them and who doesn’t. They’ll eventually find out what it means to truly be a family and they’ll rectify all the mistakes their parents made. 

But all of that comes later. 

Chapter End Notes

Thank you all for your patience. The attention this story has garnered is beyond anything I could've imagined. I hope this ending does them justice in your eyes. Thank you all for the journey <3

Chapter 10: Epilogue

Chapter Summary

Two years later, their love is stronger than ever. Agatha is ready to take the next steps, never having been more sure of anything in her entire life.

Chapter Notes

Months later and I couldn't let them go. I miss them dearly and felt entirely to soft about them to cope. So as a result, here's a proper ending to their story. A 30k epilogue to wrap things up. Thank you to all of you who have commented, liked, and shared this story. I hope you enjoy this little slice as much as I enjoyed revisiting them.

Two years later.

The sun is different this morning. Warmer in the way you can tell it’s summertime without looking at the date on the calendar. The trees, though scarce among the pavement, are greener. Their leaves are rustling in the breeze. All the windows of the skyscrapers mirror the bright blue hue of the sky with the sun glaring off of a few. 

Agatha would never say it aloud, but she’s missed this city. After spending two weeks in Greece for Rio’s brother’s wedding, she hadn’t realized how much she’d missed air conditioning and being just far enough from the equator that the air around her didn’t feel like a suffocating, humid trap. 

She settles back into work like she never left with her new assistant having kept things tidy in her absence. Though, the young assistant could only do so much and now meetings have piled up with a stack of new documents waiting for Agatha’s stamp of approval that are staring her down like some fucking stand off in the wild west, but through it all there an insistent smile on her face. And it’s not because she’s happy to be back behind her desk. Rather, she can’t shake herself of the memories of their wedding get away.

Rio and her sun-kissed skin, blonde streaks of hair from the European sun with her cheeks creasing from her gap toothed smile. All of the suits and linen shirts she’d worn that would definitely be making an appearance again if Agatha had anything to do with it. Somewhere along the way, Rio had come into her own. She'd found herself dressing more masculine, sinking into the feeling of confidence it gave her and never looking back. Agatha at up every single second of it, starving for crumb after crumb during the entirety of their stay in Greece. The way Rio looked under the moonlight at the rehearsal dinner with her shirt unbuttoned down her chest, tattooed sternum on full display making her look ethereal in the way that Agatha couldn’t look away if she tried. But most importantly, how she’d looked standing next to her brother, watching as his bride walked down the aisle and all Agatha could think about is what it would be like if she were the one walking towards Rio instead.

She could see it so clearly that it sent an ache through her chest so profound, it’s still lingering weeks later. She found herself asking questions she’d never given a second thought before. Would they have an outdoor wedding? It’s no question that Rio would look breathtaking in the soft glow of a sunset. Would it be in a forest somewhere, surrounded by the Earth colors and greenery that suited Rio all too well? Would Rio wear a suit? A dress? Agatha couldn’t care less if she wore anything at all so long as she said "I do."

The thoughts didn’t stop circling through her mind. Even as she poured her coffee, brushed her teeth or attempted to read a book at night next to the soft snores of the bane of her current predicament. It didn’t matter. The greenery is what sells them the most. They’d humored a massive estate wedding with elegance and extravagance, but neither of them found it fitting. Their love is quiet and private, something sacred to them and those they’ve let be a part of their story. 

Instead, they settle on mismatched wooden chairs and an old vintage rug leading them down the aisle. There will be eucalyptus, hydrangeas and white roses. Dishes that blend Agatha’s preference for refined cuisine with Rio’s love for comfort food. Moody florals with deep greens and midnight purples. They’ll have the reception in the same location under strung lights with a long rectangular table covered in a table cloth and flickering candles littering the surface.

They’ll dance together under those same lights and everything will somehow look nothing like Agatha had ever pictured, but everything she’d ever wished for.

After that, wedding planning somehow becomes easier and more difficult at the same time. Most would think the venue would be the toughest challenge, Agatha did, but the small tedious details prove to be worse.

Or maybe that’s just because of the company Agatha and Rio choose to bring along with them. 

On the day of the bridesmaid dress shopping, Rio ships her fiancée out of the door with a smile and a reassuring kiss despite the grimace on the older woman’s face. 

In Jen’s boutique, Wanda stands in front of the mirror holding up a bridesmaid dress that looks suspiciously like a potato sack and Agatha’s frown turns up just a little. 

“This is an attack,” the redhead announces flatly, eyes flickering to each of her friends as she looks at them incredulously, mostly to her former boss.

Jen smirks from her chair, twirling the champagne in her glass. “You’ll live. And you’ll look great. Especially when you’re standing next to me.” 

Wanda groans and stomps back towards the rack of dresses next to her. She grumbles under her breath just loud enough for them all to hear. “I know Agatha picked this just to spite me.”

“You look great, Red,” the CEO says, trying not to laugh, but failing miserably after seeing Wanda pick the next dress in line that doesn’t fare much better. Alice just records the whole thing silently in the corner with the intention of showing Rio later on. 

“Who’s next,” Wanda declares having had enough of Jen’s options and stomping down the stairs of the podium. Her friends just boo her, balling up their napkins and throwing them in her direction as she attempts to dodge all of them. 

—

Agatha and Rio wanted to have a private cake tasting, but after much deliberation, they’d asked their friends to come because there was no way just the two of them would agree on anything remotely decent. Not when they live just to spite each other. 

Jen and Wanda had agreed, Alice and Nat had agreed by extension and Matt had come when he’d asked if he could because it would be the only part of the wedding planning that he could offer his two cents into. Rio had nearly burst with excitement. 

So that’s how the seven of them ended up at a table in one of those niche little corner bakeries trying every single cake consistency and flavor combination under the sun. 

Marble had been considered.

Carrot cake was vetoed. 

Fondant icing was a hard no.

And then Matt bites into a slice of lemon cake and immediately grimaces as if he’d  been stabbed. “Absolutely not. This tastes like Pinesol.” 

Rio, who doesn’t seem to share the same sentiment, happily eats the rest of his piece. As well as Agatha’s and the older woman sighs, rubbing her temples. “This shouldn’t be this hard.”

Wanda cuts in, swallowing down a mouthful of her cake. “It’s not hard. You two just need to agree on one and then we can leave.” 

Agatha seems to jump into action, dropping her hands from her temples and then sneaks a forkful of the red velvet option in front of them. Despite her urgency to get this over with, she nearly moans. “This one.”

No one dares argue after that. 

—

In the middle of seating chart chaos, Rio has laid herself out across the dining table, using place cards like tarot. She got a pen tucked behind her ear while another one is working hard against the paper as she mutters to no one in particular, “Alice and Jen next to Sharon because Jen will lose her mind… Wanda and Nat between Bucky and the open bar… Matt and Karen in front of me so I don’t combust.” 

Agatha, who’s been mindlessly looking through color swatches the whole time, storms over, snatches the cards with a disapproving sigh. “You are not creating a night of chaos.”. 

Rio whistles as she watches her pass, eyes taking over her fiancée’s full figure. “You’re hot when you’re bossy.”

Agatha glares at her, but there’s a smile in her eyes as she takes her seat across from Rio. “You’re impossible.”

The younger woman just shrugs. “I know. But admit it, you love it.”

Agatha huffs out something between a sigh and a laugh as she taps her own pen against the sheet of monstrosity Rio had orchestrated. “I tolerate it. Barely.”

Agatha fixes Rio’s nightmare of a seating chart in ten minutes flat. 

—

A few days later, Agatha’s on the way home from her palates class when she gets a facetime call as she’s walking down the street to grab an after workout smoothie. She digs the phone from her pocket, sees Rio’s name and answers it on the third ring.

Rio’s face is immediately on her screen, smiling brightly as she reveals that gap between her teeth. 

“Hi, my love,” Agatha says softly. “How’s your fitting going?”

“I think it’s going good. I just wanted to ask you something.”

Agatha’s brow furrows. “Everything okay?”

Rio nods, “Yes, I just want to make sure you like what I picked.”

“Baby,” Agatha laughs softly. “It’s your day too. I’ll love whatever you choose.”

Rio seems to chew on the bottom of her lip, eyes distant as she rolls over something in her head. “I know, but I always worry.”

“I know you do,” the CEO cooes. “If you want me to see it, I’m not opposed, but don’t expect me to go showing you my dress.”

Rio seems to spark up at this, her eyes immediately shining as she turns the camera to show her standing in front of the boutique mirror, tugging at the soft, cream-colored linen draped over her frame. The shirt is a loose, airy, button up free-flowing in a way that moves with her body every time she shifts. The pants are brown and straight legged, landing perfectly at her ankles where she adorns brown loafers.  

Agatha had been wearing a sweet smile on her face, hopeful her girlfriend would be ready to tell her how the fitting went but the moment she catches sight of Rio on the screen, she freezes. 

Her eyes widen, pupils dark and greedy with her perfectly arched brow, lips already curling like she’s about to say something wicked. “Oh… oh, no. Absolutely not.”

Rio blinks, life seemingly leaving her eyes. “Not good?”

Agatha doesn’t even think to comfort her. She’s not even thinking about anything besides how much effort it’s going to take not to mount Rio in front of their wedding guests. She leans closer to the camera, voice dropping, velvet and low. “Not good? Darling, you expect me to stand upright and recite vows while you wear that? You look like a fucking prince charming!”

She can hear Matt chuckling in the background while the reflection shows Benny pumping a fist in the air like he’d been the sole responsible one to put this together. And then her eyes catch Rio, cheeks pink as she bites down on a smile she can’t control. “So… that’s a yes? Are you sure it’s not too casual? They have some tuxes I can try? Would you prefer I wear a dress?”

Agatha exhales sharply, trying to collect herself. “That’s a you’re walking down the aisle in that and I’m going to regret letting people watch me marry you because they’ll all know what I’m thinking.”

Benny cackles again, but this time she can’t see him. “She’s combusting! Called it!”

“But seriously, Rio. I don’t care if you walk down the aisle in a trash bag, I’m marrying you regardless.”

Rio hides her grin behind her hand, eyes shining. “Guess I found my outfit.”

“Hell yes you did,” Agatha confirms, her smile blistering. “I might kill you for wearing it, but I’ll definitely kill you if you don’t.” 

Rio giggles. “Noted, babe.”

—

When it’s Agatha’s turn, Jen’s boutique is the fitting choice of course. The room is bathed in soft afternoon light. It’s far from the mood of Agatha’s choosing, but her best friend hasn’t stopped bringing over mimosas, so she quit complaining somewhere around the third glass. There had been a few dresses so far, most far too elegant for what either of them were going for. And after seeing Rio's much more casual choice in outfit, she’d had her heart set on something flowy and comfortable. 

The first one had been too long. Second, too revealing. Third, itchy. 

But on the fourth one, Agatha steps out of the fitting room, and the moment she does, Wanda, Jen, and Alice freeze.

The dress is white of course—pure, glowing, and unapologetically sexy. The fabric hugs her perfectly, a subtle plunge in the neckline that’s just daring enough to get her fiancée’s attention. The silk flows over her hips, the skirt swaying with every step, and those white heels… oh, those heels. Sharp, impossibly tall, perfectly sculpted. They make her legs look endless.

Wanda lets out a low whistle, eyes following her friend’s every step. “Oh my god. Agatha. You look illegal.”

Alice slowly claps her hands as if she’d had a job well done, eyes wide with awe. “Rio is going to collapse and I’m so fucking excited to see it.”

“We better be married before she decides to collapse,” Agatha gripes, but there’s a smile tugging at the corners of her mouth. 

Wanda grins mischievously as she scopes out her surrounding friends, all too distracted to notice that she pulls out her phone. She seizes her moment and melts into the warm feeling of the alcohol coursing through her system. “Okay, listen. I have to call Rio. She deserves to suffer just a little.”

“No! Don’t you dare, Maximoff,” Agatha protests, swatting at her.

“Relax, I’m not going to let her see,” Wanda reassures as the phone begins to ring on speaker. “I’m just going to give her a little audible tease.”

Agatha seems to relax, but the sound of her fiancée’s voice tenses her back up. 

“Hey, babe,” Rio’s voice is casual until Wanda bursts in with barely-contained glee.

“Rio! You are so not ready for this. Agatha looks…insane. Like, oh my god! You’re not prepared!”

Rio goes silent and Agatha swears five minutes pass before she hears her partner's voice finally speak, “Oh god, she’s going to destroy me, isn’t she?”

Jen snickers in the background as Alice giggles. “Mentally brace yourself, Rio. It’s not going to be pretty for you.”

Rio groans. “This is not a fair fight.”

Wanda laughs. “Consider yourself warned.”

—

Some weeks later, it’s a late night at Agatha and Rio’s. One of the last ones as the nights before the wedding start dwindling down. The living room coffee table is covered in beer bottles, sticky notes, and half-eaten pizza. Wanda is asleep on the couch with a veil draped over her head as she half lays on Nat, half hangs off the cushions, Jen is ranting about overpriced florists, Alice is trying to prank call the caterer with Matt and Benny is telling Rio to ‘elope and save me the stress.’

The rest of the, still awake, group shush him, chastising him for missing half of the wedding prep and showing up just in time for the fun stuff. 

Agatha looks around at the chaos and, despite everything she smiles.

With the little details finally out of the way, she feels like she could make room to be excited again. There had been far too many petty arguments along the way that only made things stretch out further and further—seemingly moving the wedding backwards along with it. But thankfully with that behind them, there is only one thing left to knock off of the list…

A joint bachelorette party had been Alice’s idea. ‘Less scheduling, more drinking’ and somehow everyone agrees, despite the obvious recipe for disaster. Agatha would’ve been okay with staying at home and ordering another pizza while they all ended up wine drunk in the comfort of her home. But Rio seemed overjoyed with the idea of getting back into a club since she’d stopped bartending once she passed the bar exam. 

Naturally, Agatha caves and begrudgingly allows Wanda to take the reins on planning the night ahead of them, but by the time they arrive at the place, Agatha is already scoping the area for the nearest exits. 

It’s a hole in the wall, for a lack of a better description. The outside is a literal warehouse with big industrial windows that are giving a full view of the thrashing lights inside. The music is loud and Agatha can tell it’s going to be a night of 2000’s hits and glitter just by the look on Wanda’s face. Alice and Jen seem to be indifferent but willing and well, Matt and Benny could take it or leave it. 

But Rio, she’s beaming like there’s no place she’d rather be. 

So Agatha swallows her complaints and focuses on the way Rio’s hand fits in hers, squeezing just enough to keep her grounded. She lets Rio guide her through the doors and the droves of people that shuffle around them. Normally she’d be halfway to a panic attack, but Rio keeps looking back at her with reassurance as she guides them with their hands still connected and arms outstretched. Agatha couldn’t tell you what song has been playing or how many people they’ve passed, but she could tell you how many times Rio's blinked in the last minute. Her smile is blinding, hair framing her face beautifully and there’s nothing in this moment that matters more than sinking into the feeling of comfort only her fiancée brings her. 

They get to a private corner of the place that’s roped off with a glittery sign propped up in the middle of the table that says ‘reserved.’ It’s nothing more than a lounge area with a few couches and a table or two, but it’s enough space for them to definitely do some damage.  Wanda swoops in and removes the tacky velvet rope so that they can invade the space. There’s a table in the center with a bucket of ice holding a bottle of champagne, a few glasses on a charger next to it. 

It’s no surprise that they all rush to the alcohol. Agatha’s. not sure who gets their hands on the bottle first, but She does know that Wanda ends up with it. She makes a pointed effort to pop open the cork away from everyone and then equally distributes it into the glasses so that everyone can have one. The CEO knows what’s happening before she can stop it. 

“I said no fucking speeches,” Agatha barks towards her friends immediately, but Rio just smacks her shoulder lightly. She’s not a fan of the sappy declarations of love. Especially when she’s trying to have a fun night out. The last thing she needs is an existential crisis. 

“Yes, but lucky for you, this is a toast,” Wanda corrects her as she raises her own glass, the others following suit. Begrudgingly, Agatha raises hers. “To Agatha and Rio. May they always be happy together,  forever.”

The older woman gripes again, but her heart flutters despite it. And when Rio wraps her arm around her waist and pulls their bodies together, she lets herself relax. 

By midnight, Wanda and Alice are locked in a serious competition to out dance each other to Promiscuous, and Agatha and Jen are trying not to burst into a fit of laughter though the alcohol in their systems makes it much harder to resist. Especially when Wanda has somehow ended up with a feather boa and Alice is on her third failed attempt to do the worm.

On the other side of the space, Rio’s with Benny and Matt as they have declared it their sacred duty to keep her glass full. Agatha’s taken notice of the fact that her fiancee has been slowly sipping her drinks throughout the night as though to be respectful of her brother and best friend’s wallets. Agatha makes a mental note to take care of the tab for everyone, but for now, she just approaches Rio and settles down onto the couch beside her. 

The younger woman greets her with a relaxed, warm smile, immediately sliding over so that she can saddle up next to her and close any space between them. On the other side of her fiancee is Benny and he’s animatedly swinging his glass in the air as he slings his free arm around Rio like he hasn’t already toasted her seventeen times. “To my sister and to my soon-to-be sister-in-law, who’s terrifying, by the way.” 

He raises his drink toward Agatha, who arches one perfectly unimpressed eyebrow before sipping her martini with a glare. She’s not sure if that was meant to be a compliment, but with the way Benny is smiling, she knows it’s genuine. Rio only affirms that when she slides her hand over Agatha’s thigh and squeezes lightly, her  ring glinting on her finger. 

“You have no idea how terrifying,” Matt tells Benny, following his admission with a swig of his whiskey. Agatha draws her attention back to the other parties, unamused at Matt’s interjection.

“Oh yeah. Wasn’t she your boss at one point?”

“Unfortunately,” Matt confirms, his words slurring.

“Unfortunately,” Agatha echoes back with a gasp, her hand covering her chest. 

Rio’s voice pipes up beside her. “I love you, but working for you is a nightmare, honey,” 

Rio is laughing, her cheeks flushed. She’s got that reckless kind of joy that only shows up when she’s tipsy and surrounded by people she loves. Agatha’s mock annoyance doesn’t last for long as she dissolves into her own fit of laughter, pointing at her two previous employees. “Yeah, well, you two were my biggest headache. I couldn’t keep you in line.”

“That’s not what my recommendation letter from you said,” Matt chirps, a smile hiding behind his glass as Agatha cuts him another deserving glare. Rio giggles, stifling it behind her hand as Agatha shoots her the same disapproving look. 

“Okay you two,” Rio pipes up, smacking her legs as she stands from her seat, looking over towards her two friends across from them. “How about we dance?”

Matt and Benny are quick to hop up in agreement, but Agatha opts to stay behind and finish her martini with the added show of Jen, Alice, and Wanda now forming a dance routine. Rio gives her a quick kiss on the top of her head before she saunters off behind the two guys, already wiggling her body behind them in excitement.

Agatha watches her fiancée in awe, missing her touch as the distance between them grows. Rio seems to melt right into the dance floor as soon as they fold into the crowd, Matt and Benny on either of her sides so as to keep her from any lingering creeps. The gesture makes Agatha’s heart swell.  This family they’d built is far more than anything she ever thought she deserved. She’s not sure she’ll ever get used to having them, but she knows they won’t accept any other option. 

She’d meant to stay seated, really. But it’s impossible not to look. Rio catches the colored lights every time she spins, smiling faintly as she laughs at something Matt says, one hand in the air, the other balancing against Benny’s shoulder. They’re guarding her in that easy, brotherly way that’s never too close and always keeping a respectful circle, but Rio commands the space all the same. She looks so free that Agatha’s chest aches.

It’s ridiculous how quickly she misses her. She can still feel the ghost of that quick kiss on her hair, but it’s not enough. Never is.

By the time she finishes her drink, her resolve is gone. She sets the empty glass down and mutters something under her breath that sounds suspiciously like fuck it. The crowd parts for her easily enough. Her focus is locked on the woman at the center of it all. The woman she’s going to marry. Rio spots her halfway through a spin, her grin widening instantly as she reaches out both hands in invitation

Agatha takes them without hesitation. She always will.

Rio loops her arms around Agatha’s neck, eyes bright. “Hey you.”

Agatha smirks, fingers settling on Rio’s waist, warm against the sliver of her exposed hipbone. “I missed you.”

Rio hums, tilting her head. “You saw me five minutes ago.”

“And I missed you for all five of them.”

That earns her a grin so wide it could split her face.

“You’re awfully romantic tonight,” Rio laughs, raising a brow in curiosity. Agatha just waves her off with a tsk of her tongue, but the younger woman immediately pulls her attention back in with a gently guided hand on the back of her neck. Their eyes connect slowly despite the thrashing music and lights around them. She moves forward to connect their lips in a kiss that’s soft and slow and everything Agatha has been hoping for.

When they part the words are burning on her tongue. 

“I just really love you,” Agatha whispers between them, her breath puffing against Rio’s lips. “I can’t wait to marry you. Every second you’re not my wife feels like torture.” 

She can hear Rio’s sharp intake of breath as she swallows thickly. “Agatha, if you keep saying things like that, we’re adding another bathroom to the tally.”

The older woman laughs. “I wouldn’t be opposed.”

Rio just shakes her head. “Well, I would. That bathroom is filthy and I’m not getting a tetanus shot on Monday because you scraped my ass against the rusty stall door.”

Agatha laughs with a snort, head tilted back and eyes nearly closed as the happiness envelops her whole. She doesn’t see it, but Rio just stares at her in awe, no doubt, thinking about how she too can’t wait to marry her other half. 

Though they had planned to leave much earlier, they stay until the last call hits and their table looks like an absolute war zone with half-empty bottles, abandoned glasses with melting ice, and one lone tiara that Rio refuses to take off. (They’d stolen it from a bachelorette party next to them).

Wanda is sprawled across two chairs, mumbling about how she’s ‘definitely still hot enough to be a bridesmaid.’ Jen is trying to herd her up like a sheepdog, muttering curses under her breath as Alice tries and fails to be of any help. She’s far too drunk to keep her balance and keeps latching onto Jen for support and causing the short haired woman to lose her grip on the redhead. Benny just shakes his head at the sight, defeated and muttering, “This is why I drink slow.”

Through it all, Agatha keeps one hand on Rio’s thigh, protective and steadying, even as her fiancée is giggling nonstop at nothing in particular and starts making comments about things Agatha can’t even begin to understand. She reassures Rio anyway and lies about knowing who a certain video game character is, but she knows her fiancee won’t remember the betrayal in the morning. 

When the group finally stumbles out into the cool night air, chaos reigns. Wanda’s finally up on her two feet, Alice clinging to her as if she’d be of any help. Jen immediately starts singing ‘Going to the Chapel’ at the top of her lungs as if the first rendition wasn’t enough and Wanda joins in two keys too high while Matt pretends to conduct them like a choir as Benny guides him through the streets, cheering them on as a one man crowd. 

Rio, tiara crooked, clings to Agatha’s arm and laughs so hard she nearly trips over thin air, but the older woman catches her with an ease that almost looks practiced. When Agatha pulls Rio back onto her feet, it’s only a second later that Agatha walks Rio backwards and presses her against the brick wall of the bar’s exterior. Her mouth is on Rio’s, slow and hungry this time, savoring her instead of rushing. Rio melts instantly, arms around her neck, tiara nearly falling off as she kisses back like they’re the only two people in the city.

The others are too busy bickering about calling cabs to notice until Jen spins around midway through her song, catching two shadowy figures hiding next to the street light. She’s pointing at them when she screams “Hey. They’re at it again!”

A chorus of groans and laughter echoes through the street with Benny covering his eyes. “I’m serious, I need hazard pay for seeing my sister do these things.”

Agatha reluctantly pulls back, tucking a lock of Rio’s hair behind her ear and finding it hard to tear herself away when the look in Rio’s eyes keeps drawing her back in. “Let’s go home before they make a scene.”

Rio beams at her, eyes half-lidded, tiara glittering in the streetlight. “I think we’re the ones making a scene, my love.”

Agatha chuckles, linking their fingers tight as she guides her toward the waiting cab. “Trust me, baby. If we were to make a scene, they’d know it.”

Rio’s laugh echoes down the street, warm and giddy, as their friends stumble into the cab in front of them, still singing, but for Agatha and Rio the night feels like it belongs only to them.

As expected, the ride home is a mess. Wanda falls asleep on Alice’s shoulder almost immediately. Jen won’t stop harmonizing with herself and Matt and Benny argue over which pizza place they need to stop at before going home.

But Agatha and Rio barely hear any of it. Rio is curled into Agatha’s side, tiara still perched like a crown of victory with her giggles muffled into Agatha’s neck as Agatha kisses the crown of her head. Rio steadily places warm kisses against the nape of the older woman’s neck as Agatha whispers “Not in front of your brother,” which only makes Rio do it again.

When they finally stumble into their house, the front door slams shut behind them with a bang. Rio kicks off her heels immediately, one flying into the corner, the other skittering across the hardwood to most likely never be discovered again.

“We’re finally free,” Agatha says, but she’s already laughing, grabbing Rio before they both topple over.

Rio hooks her arms around Agatha’s neck, pulling her down for a sloppy, heated kiss as they walk backwards into the living room. Agatha holds her waist tightly, keeping them as steady as she can.

“God, I love you,” Rio breathes, lips brushing against Agatha’s and she just kisses her like she’s been waiting all night for this exact moment. 

“You drive me insane,” she mutters between kisses, her hands sliding under the hem of Rio’s shirt, fingertips grazing warm skin and sending goosebumps along the way. Rio gasps, tugging at Agatha’s jacket until it falls to the floor in a heap. 

“Insane enough to marry me?” Rio teases, eyes glinting with mischief as she tears Agatha’s shirt over her head.

Agatha raises her arms to compile happily as she bites at her lower lip, groaning. “Insane enough to marry you twice if I could.”

Rio grins drunkenly at that, tipping her head back as Agatha kisses down her throat, leaving trails of heat with every press of her mouth. Their path gets less steady as they begin knocking into furniture, laughing too hard and too wildly to care. A lamp nearly topples when Agatha pushes Rio back onto the couch, straddling her. The tiara slides down her head and she rips it off, tossing it across the room without looking.

Agatha stares down at her, hair wild, lipstick smudged, with her chest rising fast and for a moment, she forgets every ounce of chaos from earlier. All she sees is the woman she loves more than anything laid beneath her, ready for absolutely anything as they remain tangled together on their couch like the night was always meant to end this way.

—

The next time they see their friends is after their flights have landed and they arrive in the rental home Agatha had picked for them all to stay in for the duration of the wedding. It’d been something she’d found on a whim, a cabin overlooking the coast that was most likely far too elegant for any of their friends to be trusted in, but just perfect enough to make due for the time crunch she was in. 

Agatha and Rio arrived last as they both needed to tidy a few things up at their jobs before they left for the next week or so. It’d taken a lot longer than either of them expected, but they made it to the venue for rehearsal just short of an hour early. 

Despite the rowdiness of their group, they finish in record time and safely arrive back at the cabin just in time for a dinner that is to be prepared by a hired chef. Agatha clearly pulled out all of the stops for their found family as they spend their time reminiscing over the last few months that have led up to this. While they wait for it to be plated, the group circles around a small fire pit on the outside deck, music playing, glasses of wine in hand and a glint in their eyes that says they couldn’t be happier to be exactly where they are at this moment.

Rio’s arms are wrapped around Agatha from behind as they look out into the orange sky over the ocean. Wanda is curled into Nat, Jen and Alice mirroring the same position. Matt and Karen as well as Benny and his wife are sitting next to each other at the table talking about something Agatha can't quite bring herself to care enough about. 

When she pictured this moment years ago, it looked a lot different with much less intimacy and far more rehearsed politeness for Ralph and her mother’s sake. But now, with a cool ocean breeze in her hair and the smell of her fiancée’s earthy shampoo filling her nose, she’s glad she never gave that thought a chance. 

“I can’t wait to marry you,” Agatha says earnestly, her head falling back onto Rio’s shoulder so that she can connect their eyes. The younger woman cracks a smile with her tongue poking against her cheek.

“One more day,” she says as she leans down and nestles herself against Agatha’s temple.

The older woman echoes her words like a promise. “One more day.” 

They eat their prepared dinner at the table outside on the porch. There’s flickering candles as the center piece and seemingly never ending glasses of wine appearing one after the other. It turns out to be the best steak any of them have ever had per Rio’s declaration, but Matt swears the mashed potatoes top everything. Rio just thinks he likes to disagree with her on purpose.

Wanda, already a little unsteady from the wine, lifts her glass with dramatic flourish. “Alright, bets. How long tomorrow before they sneak off together? Ten minutes after the first dance? Fifteen?”

Jen doesn’t miss a beat, leaning lazily back in her chair. “Please. Dinner won’t even be served before they disappear.”

Rio nearly chokes on her drink, face burning as the table dissolves into laughter. “We’re right here!”

Agatha, of course, doesn’t flinch. She only crosses her legs elegantly, one arm draped along the back of her chair, and purrs with maddening calm, “They’re not wrong, darling.”

The table breaks out into a fit of laughter. Rio drops her face into her hands, groaning while Agatha smirks proudly beside her, clearly enjoying every second of her fiancée’s torment.

The wine flows, the candles burn lower, and the laughter carries into every corner of the surrounding sea. The table dissolves into a comforting silence, each and everyone letting their food settle as their empty plates are cleared from in front of them, wine glasses nearly in an identical state. The waves crashing against the shore mixes with the soft background noise of what sounds like a 60’s romcom soundtrack. The air tastes like salt and smoke. The moment feels like it could never end, until Jen stands up from her seat, half empty glass in hand. 

Agatha’s biting her tongue and halfway to opening her mouth when Jen is quick to cut her off. 

“I don’t care if you give me that look, Agatha,” Jen is quick to say as fondly as she can, but her eyes carry a weighted seriousness that Agatha doesn’t press. “I’ve waited for this day for you for a long time. And not just this day, but the day where you finally let someone love you the way that you always deserved.”

The CEO swallows thickly as the candle light casts shadows softly along her face, threatening to reveal the swell of emotion beginning to pool in her eyes. 

“You’ve been my best friend longer than I can remember. I’ve seen you ace an exam without cracking a book, talk circles around CEOs, especially Tony Stark,” There’s a round of chuckles. “You silence rooms with just one look, but I’ve never seen you the way you are with Rio.”

There’s a weighted pause, one that says far more than anything else that could leave Jen’s mouth at this moment. Agatha has to look away in favor of keeping herself from blinking out her tears. She finds Rio looking at her, completely unguarded in the way the younger woman always is around her. Her eyes are bright with the candles reflecting in her irises and she’s smiling like there’s no one else in the room. She reaches for Agatha’s hand under the table as if on instinct and starts rubbing her thumb against the back of it.

“The way you two love each other is magnetic. Everyone around you can feel it. I’m sure everyone at this table can vouch for me when I say it’s sickening,” There’s a round of chuckles and a loud woop from Benny as his wife smacks him softly against his shoulder. “But seriously Agatha. I told you three years ago that you deserved this. Before I even knew Rio. Before I even knew what you two would become for each other, I could see what she did to you. She brought out the real you. She gave me my insufferable best friend back.”

Jen’s eyes are pooling with tears as she finds Agatha’s, both of them mirroring one another as they shine with unshed tears and the promise of always fighting for this friendship, no matter the obstacle. And then Jen looks to Rio which is something Agatha hadn’t expected. “And to you, Rio, Thank you. Thank you for loving her and being patient with her. You match her crazy completely. I would say you bring her back down to Earth, but that’s just not true. She yanks you up above us all with her.”

Agatha is nodding along, tears streaming down her cheeks as Rio keeps her menstruations against the back of her hand, soaking in every single reaction on Agatha’s face. Jen raises her glass in the air, all of their friends following suit as she finally rounds off her speech and the older woman feels like she can’t breathe. “To the two people on this planet most suited for each other, Agatha and Rio. I love you both.”

There’s sounds of glasses clinking, noses being blown and laughter through streaming tears. But what rings the loudest is Agatha’s voice as she abruptly stands up from her chair, the legs screeching against the wood. “What the fuck was that, Jen?”

And then she’s shuffling over to Jen with her arms wide and a smile on her face that’s so rarely ever seen by anyone besides her fiancee. Wanda’s secretly filming it from across the table, her own tears clouding her vision as Nat holds her steady with an arm around her shoulders. 

No one follows that up. They couldn’t if they tried, but Matt says that his speech will surely give it a run for its money tomorrow. Rio just leans over towards him and runs a playful hand through his hair before giving his head a light shove. “I don’t need a speech, you idiot. You being here is enough.”

“Just you wait,” Matt promises, leaning over and placing a kiss towards the crown of Rio’s head.

The night wraps up pretty quickly after that. All of them excited for tomorrow. Mostly everyone says goodnight to each other and then disappears into their respective rooms, but Agatha catches Rio’s wrist before she can go inside and offers her a faint smile. “Come here.”

Agatha’s fingers are threaded loosely with Rio’s, and instead of releasing her, she tugs. No words at first, just that familiar pull of Rio’s unguarded love. They slip onto the deck where the chatter fades to a murmur and the stars take the place of chandeliers. The night air carries the scent of salt and embers as the smoke from the dying fire tangles between them. 

Rio settles into Agatha’s arms, the weight of the night finally falling from her shoulders as she slips into a quiet sigh. “Tomorrow doesn’t even feel real. Like I’ll wake up and it’ll all be gone.”

Agatha lifts her hand, cupping Rio’s cheek and steadying her with gentle passes of her thumb. “I’m not going anywhere.”

And then the music shifts from the tired speakers by the patio doors. The unmistakable sound of one of Agatha’s favorite songs travels faintly through the air, Stay… just a little bit longer…

Agatha’s face lights up, her smile almost contagious as she gets a glint in her eye that tells Rio she’s up to something that only one of them will benefit from. Rio laughs, covering her face with one hand as she watches Agatha start to pull her backwards into the open space of the patio, her hips swaying as she steps. “No way. Absolutely not.”

Agatha’s smirk sharpens. “Please, my love?”

“Agatha, I don’t—” Rio starts, but she’s already moving, already being pulled into the familiar rhythm that only Agatha can make her comfortable enough to fall into. The older woman positions Rio with precision, one hand at her hip, the other linked tightly with hers. They move with quick steps, a playful rock to their feet as they find the shag’s easy swing. Rio stumbles a few times at first, laughing so hard she nearly loses the beat, but Agatha steadies her. 

“Relax,” Agatha murmurs, her eyes glittering with promise as she keeps their gaze locked together. “Just follow me.”

So Rio does. God she would follow this woman anywhere. 

The steps fall into place just as Agatha promised they would. Side to side, a little twist, it doesn’t matter. Rio handles them all with a dignified grace multiplied by the confidence Agatha had given her. Their feet are brushing in sync as the song wraps around them. Agatha’s hair swings with the motion, her laugh spilling into the night, and Rio just watches her like she’s trying to freeze the moment for later. 

“You’re ridiculous,” Rio pants, trying not to trip.

“Says the woman tripping over her own two feet,” Agatha returns, spinning her just enough to make her stumble and crash back into her arms.

The deck creaks beneath them, the stars wide and watching. They keep moving even when the song fades, a slower sway now, a lazy echo of the shag as they hold each other in the quiet. Their steps are slower now, easing into a sway that barely moves them across the deck. Rio’s cheek finds Agatha’s shoulder, her smile pressed into fabric as Agatha’s hand stays steady on her waist, the other laced firm with her fingers.

Won’t you say you love me all of the time?

For a long moment, the world feels suspended. Just the two of them, the stars above, the faint hum of the night until Rio finally whispers, “I don’t want to let you go.”

“I know, but we have to,” Agatha murmurs back, her lips brushing her temple as she places a soft kiss to the skin there, nuzzling in her nose. “At least for tonight.”

Rio tilts her head up, eyes wide and almost childlike. “I hate it. We’ve not done one traditional thing this whole relationship, but this is what you’re adamant about?”

“Remember the Christmas tree, my dear,” Agatha’s smile softens, the smirk stripped away in favor of tenderness. “Plus, I know that if I sleep with you tonight, It’ll be harder for me to leave you tomorrow.”

Rio laughs, though her throat catches with emotion. “I know, but that doesn’t mean I have to be happy about it.”

Agatha dips her backwards just enough to draw another breathless laugh from her fiancée, before pulling her back close. “There’s nothing wrong with a little yearning, my love.”

The music has stopped entirely, but they linger in the silence, swaying to the echo of it. The stars are out in full force, the moon glitters against the pacific ocean and the moment feels like it could never end. Like they could stay suspended in time together, swaying to a beat only they can hear as they melt into each other

Eventually though, Rio exhales, heavy and reluctant. “I should go to bed now. Tomorrow will come faster.”

Agatha hums out a laugh as she tucks a strand of hair behind Rio’s ear, pressing a kiss to her forehead while lingering there to whisper “Go to sleep and dream of me in white.”

Rio groans. “You’re cruel.”

“And you love it.”

They part slowly, fingers slipping apart last of all. Rio backs toward the door, eyes never leaving Agatha’s, her smile trembling with both nerves and sadness. Agatha stays on the deck, poised and watching her like a promise she already owns.

“See you down the aisle,” Agatha says softly.

Rio’s grin splits wide, helpless, before she vanishes inside. Agatha tips her head back to gaze at the stars and for once she allows herself to feel it—the dizzy, terrifying, impossible joy of being completely undone by someone as imperfectly perfect for her as Rio Vidal. Tomorrow she marries her. She finally declares the love they’ve built as unshakable and she can’t fucking wait. 

She loses track of how long she’s still there, hands tucked together, gaze tilted skyward like she’s trying to commit every piece of this night to memory. She keeps replaying every moment of their love story over in her mind, choking down the emotion in her throat when she remembers just how sure of Rio she’s always been. How she could never fight off her feelings, even when she tried so desperately to. Rio always had her. And now she always will. 

She startles slightly when a deep voice clears it’s throat. She snatches her head forward to the intrusion and then relaxes when she sees it’s Benny. He’s standing just outside the patio doors, rocking back and forth on his feet as if he were teetering on deciding whether to approach or not. 

“Didn’t mean to sneak up,” he says, his voice softer than usual. “I just… I couldn’t walk past without saying something.”

Agatha tilts her head, curious. “About?”

“Her. You. The two of you.” He scratches the back of his neck, searching for words. “I’ve seen my sister happy before, sure. But not like this. When she’s with you, it’s different. It’s steady. Real.”

Agatha swallows, caught off guard by the warmth of it. “She’s the love of my life.”

A smile breaks across Benny’s face, quick and unguarded. “Yeah. I can see that. Anyone could.” 

He shakes his head a little, like he’s still marveling at it. “I guess I just wanted you to know… I’m glad it’s you. I couldn’t want more for her than what I saw out here tonight.”

The words land heavy and gentle at once, and Agatha feels her throat tighten. “That means a lot coming from you. She thinks the world of you, Benito.”

He pauses for a moment, his eyes glistening with the weight of the emotions he’s carrying. He walks over to Agatha, leaning against the railing beside her as he too looks up to the stars like he’s looking for something… maybe answers.

“I wish I hadn’t wasted so much time with her.”

It’s earnest. It’s honest. Agatha lends her ear like she has done to Rio a thousand times because by extension, she’s standing here too. 

“Our parents… I shouldn’t have let them come between us,” He says with his voice wet with emotion, eyes blinking away tears. “I know I hurt her and part of me feels guilty for even standing here as a part of her day.”

“Benito, no,” Agatha is quick to add, her body turning towards him. He turns his head to her, eyes shining with tears. She places a reassuring hand on his shoulder, rubbing the fabric of his shirt with her thumb. “She wants you here. More than anything.”

“I don’t know why,” he scoffs but it’s lighthearted. “She deserves a better brother than me.”

“And she deserves a better wife than me,” the older woman says softly. He looks at her incredulously. “But she doesn’t want one. She wants me… so I stopped beating myself up over it and let her choose me. Let her choose you… because she wants to.”

He nods, an understanding settling over his body as Agatha can see him visibly relax next to her. She's not sure when she got so good at this talking thing, but part of her feels proud. 

“Thank you,” he says softly. “I know this is you guys day, but I really needed to hear that.”

Agatha smiles. “Anytime.”

Benny sighs and then lets the night stretch easily between them. The sounds of waves crashing settles between them with the quiet chirp of a few crickets, but the moment never gets stale.

“Tomorrow’s gonna be a good day,” he finally says, and there’s no doubt in his voice.

“The best day of my life,” Agatha says earnestly, no doubt in her voice either.

“Gross,” Benny says for old times sake, a chuckle falling from his lips. 

Agatha pushes his shoulder softly. “Let’s get to bed… Your sister will kill us if we oversleep because we’re too tired.”

They both filter back inside, leaving to their respective rooms, but not before smiling softly in each other direction as there’s an unspoken understanding between them now. Both understand wasted time and the feeling of not deserving Rio’s love, but with each of them there to hold each other up, they’ll be okay. 

When Agatha wakes, she’s alone for the first time in years. She didn’t sleep as well as she’d hoped, but she was able to get a few hours of rest as opposed to none. Keeping herself away from Rio proved harder than she thought, but it’s the one thing about weddings she really loved. The separation only makes reuniting sweeter.

Agatha hadn’t bargained for the silence that swarmed her in the quiet of the night. She thought about her and Benny’s talk and how Rio is lucky enough to have a sibling that cares for her the way he does. 

She’s not sure how, but Agatha had started to care that she would be the only one with Harkness blood to be at her own wedding. She had absolutely no one. And normally that’s okay. She’d accepted awards alone. Attended events alone, but the thought hit her so suddenly at two in the morning that she’d nearly caved and crawled into bed with Rio. 

Her heart ached for that connection for the first time in years. And now she’s awake with one singular thought on her mind. She misses her fiancée and the comfort only she can bring. She thinks about calling her, but decides against it and right as she is about to pull herself out of the bed, the door to the room flings open abruptly and reveals a disheveled red head. “You better be by yourself in here, Harkness.”

Agatha looks at her friend in disbelief as Wanda sweeps the room with her eyes in search for the finest thing out of place. 

“I think we’re clear guys,” Wanda announces to her entourage behind her, before throwing out her last words to Agatha as she shuts the door. “Get up! It’s your wedding day, bitch.”

The older woman grumbles as she sits upright in her bed, hair tangled every which way and an ache in her bones from the unfamiliar mattress. The morning light spills softly through the curtains and the warmth hits her body making her want to immediately fall back asleep. She doesn’t let herself go back to sleep, but she doesn’t make a quick effort to move either. She lets the sun warm her body, enveloping it in a warmth that brings a comforting smile to her lips. In just a few short hours, she’d have a wife. She’d be someone’s wife. Rio’s wife. 

And that’s all that matters. 

A beat passes before Jen appears in the doorway with a soft smile and two mimosa glasses, one in each hand. “When you’re ready, the girls are out here waiting. Rio's upstairs and we have downstairs.”

Agatha nods along. She takes the glass wordlessly, tipping it back against her lips and nearly downs it in one go.

Jen furrows her brows, picking up on her best friend’s demeanor easily. “Are you okay? I figured you’d be less brooding and more ‘bridezilla’ by now.”

Agatha scoffs. “There’s only one bridezilla here and it’s neither of the brides to be.”

“Wanda is definitely… a bit much this morning,” Jen giggles as she takes a seat on the bed next to her best friend. The older woman scoots over begrudgingly. “I made her mimosa with barely any orange juice.”

Agatha shakes her head, but she’s smiling. “Make sure you keep ‘em coming because it’s going to take a lot more than one to calm her down.”

“That’s why she’s already on her third,” Jen says with a wink as she clinks their empty glasses together. “Now, are you going to tell me what’s bothering you or am I going to have to ‘mimosa’ it out of you?”

The older woman laughs, an obvious attempt to brush it off, but Jen doesn’t bite. She stares onto Agatha with pleading eyes far more demanding than soft. Agatha sighs softly, her eyes falling to her empty glass as she stares absentmindedly running her finger around the rim. “It’s nothing, really. It’s stupid.”

A beat of silence passes and nothing is said. Agatha briefly thinks Jen has dropped it until their eyes meet again and the younger woman is just staring expectantly with wide eyes. Agatha gives. 

“Okay, okay. I’m just a little sad that I have no family here,” the older woman confesses, her eyes finding the rim of the glass again. “I mean, I always knew they wouldn’t be here, but I guess it didn’t hit me until last night that I would have no one.”

Jen reaches out with a hand and places it over the one that’s tracing the glass. She squeezes softly, reassuringly as she speaks, “You have us. I know that you know that and that’s not what you meant, but screw anyone, blood or otherwise, that passed up the opportunity to know you, Agatha.”

The older woman nods her head. “I know that. I just… Do you think Rio could’ve changed my mom? Would she… you know, finally be proud of me?”

Jen’s eyes almost widen comically as if she’d expected anything else and sort of Agatha regrets saying anything at all. And then Jen is reaching out and taking her hand so that it’s firm in her own. Her eyes are sharp and serious as she says, “I think that whatever that woman would’ve thought should be far away from this wedding.” 

Agatha nods, but it’s not as sure as she’d like. Jen doesn’t let it slide. “Agatha, your mother was impossible to please and what she would’ve thought about Rio wouldn’t have changed anything. She didn’t deserve to be your mother. She didn’t deserve to know Rio or your love for her.”

This time when Agatha shakes her head, it’s much more firm because her best friend is right. The truth of the matter is that her mom would’ve most likely ruined whatever she and Rio had. They both are far better without her. 

“Is it stupid that I just wish I had Rio here to tell me it’s going to be okay? I’ve been away from her one night and I have this emotional crisis that makes me miss her far more than I should.”

Jen laughs softly. “You want to see her?”

“No, Wanda would kill me,” Agatha is quick to add with a hollow laugh. “I just wish I would’ve never made us sleep in separate rooms. I was just trying to be romantic.”

Jen nods understandingly, pausing for a moment as if to digest a thought. And then she finally speaks, “Wait here okay? Do not open the door. Whatever you do.”

The older woman nods though she’s understandably confused as she watches Jen exit the room and close the door behind her.
