There’s a few minutes that pass and Agatha starts to get concerned, her mind filled with doubts as she is left alone in the silence of the room. And then there’s a soft knock followed by a voice that would quiet her loudest storms. “Baby?”

The relief floods Agatha’s system almost immediately as she crashes towards the door, her hands melting to the surface as if she could feel Rio on the other side if she pressed hard enough. “Rio?”

“Who else would call you baby,” Rio laughs. “Should I be worried there’s someone else? Is this why you’re getting cold feet all of a sudden?”

Agatha is quick to jump in, “I’m not getting cold feet! Who told you that?”

“No one,” Rio says softly, though her voice wavers with a worry only Agatha could pick up on. “I’m just worried that’s what this is. Jen said you were panicking.”

“Christ, she’s so dramatic,” Agatha scoffs, her forehead thudding against the door as she laughs humorlessly. “I’m not panicking, love. I just… needed to hear your voice. Just to make sure this is real.”

Rio seems to sigh in relief, a thud sounding from her side of the door as well and Agatha likes to imagine them both leaning against this door, desperate for each other's touch. “It’s so real, Agatha. I’m wearing my outfit and I cried when I put it on like the biggest loser ever. Benny has a video, so you’ll get to see it… But I can’t wait to see you, Agatha. I bet you look so beautiful.”

Agatha’s eyes feather closed, a smile gracing her lips. “I can’t wait for you to see it either.”

“You want to know a secret,” Rio asks softly. “I also can’t wait to take it off of you.” 

Agatha giggles, her body seemingly getting lighter by the second. “Is this where you tell me it’ll look better on the floor?”

“I’m not that corny,” Rio laughs and the sound echoes through Agatha’s head, filling her with enough confidence to carry on. There’s a lingering pause though. One that opens a pot of concern in Agatha’s chest as she leans her ear against the door, worried Rio had left, but she can hear the soft sound of Rio’s fingers rhythmically tapping against the wood. She’s halfway to asking if she’s okay when the younger woman’s voice sounds out. “Are you sure you want to do this? I won’t be mad if you back out.”

Agatha nearly gasps. “Rio, I’m so ready to marry you.”

“I’m just double checking,” There’s a sigh of relief and Agatha can imagine the smile on Rio’s face as she says, “You promise me you’re okay?”

“Yeah, I just missed you.”

“Aren’t you the one that separated us last night,” Rio laughs softly and the sound makes Agatha’s chest flutter despite the annoyance at Rio’s challenge. 

“I was trying to be romantic…” The older woman continues and she breathes a deep sigh of relief, immediately feeling the tension leave her bones. 

“Well now you don’t have to worry about ever sleeping away from me again,” Rio confirms.

“Okay then. I’m going to go get ready,” Agatha says softly, pausing for a moment before adding. “I love you.”

Rio doesn’t hesitate. “I love you too. See you soon. I’ll be waiting.” 

The thought gives Agatha chills as she listens to the sound of Rio’s footsteps getting further away. When they disappear entirely, Agatha steps away from the door and finds that it’s thrusted open again to reveal her friends barging in with their robes on and hair already fixed neatly. 

“Alright, ladies,” Wanda says, hands on her hips with the authority of someone who has wrangled more than a few crises this morning. “Let’s get our bride into her armor.”

“Makeup first and then dress,” Jen exclaims, bursting through the door with excitement and nearly toppling over her friends as she pushes to get close to Agatha. The older woman feigns annoyance, but her chest fills with something he’s growing all too familiar with these days—love.

She lets her friends coat her face with an unnatural amount of makeup until she makes a pointed effort to “accidentally” sneeze and wipe her face against her arm. They have to remove all the progress they’ve done, but Agatha tells them to just keep it natural this time around—something she totally didn’t plan. 

They add some light mascara, a base layer of foundation and give her a quick pass of eyeshadow that brings out the blue of her eyes. There’s hushed curses and elbows knocking each other left and right, but somehow they get it done, smiling onto Agatha like she’s their first place prize.

“Okay, now the dress,” Jen whispers under her breath. 

Alice backs away to retrieve it from its spot hanging on the closet door. She lets out a sigh, her fingertips brushing along the silk fabric of the gown as if trying to memorize the moment herself. “It’s even more gorgeous than I remembered.”

Jen lifts the hanger, steadying the weight of the dress as she carries it over to Agatha with a steady smile.

“You ready?” she asks, meeting Agatha’s eyes.

The older woman nods, her throat tight, but now more sure than ever. “As I’ll ever be.”

Together, they guide her into it. Alice and Wanda holding the skirts out so the fabric doesn’t brush the floor, Jen carefully easing it into place. It’s not a grand dress by any means. It’s more of a silk evening gown, but Agatha knows her friends are just as eager to be a part of the process as she is eager to get it over either. There’s a hush as they work, broken only by Wanda muttering about how her elbows keep crashing into Jen’s, Alice’s laughter when Agatha swears under her breath impatiently. They should’ve learned from the makeup routine, but they’ve never been good at it. 

When the dress is finally on, Wanda and Alice step back with audible gasps, admiring their best friend, but mostly their hard work. Agatha turns toward the mirror, her breath catching at the reflection staring back. It’s…her. And not just the wedding version of her she’d always thought she would be, it’s the her she always hoped to be. Casual and relaxed, no veil or poofy dress as her mother stands behind her approvingly, 

“Agatha,” Alice whispers, pressing a hand to her heart. “You look...”

Wanda’s eyes soften, her focus melting. “Rio’s going to faint the second she sees you.”

Jen stays quiet at first, her gaze steady on Agatha and the older woman takes the moment to break the attention on her with a light teasing. “Getting all emotional there Jennifer?”

“Oh please. I’m just admiring my handiwork. That dress did come from my shop by the way, so I’m like ninety percent responsible for this look.” Jen says, but she sits for just a moment, and then finally her lips curve into a soft smile, voice low with emotion. “You do look beautiful though… better than I ever imagined.” 

Agatha’s lips part, her smirk faltering into something more vulnerable. She turns from the mirror to face them, her closest people, her chosen family. “Thank you. For helping me… for being here. I don’t think I could do this without you guys.”

Wanda snorts, dabbing at the corner of her eye. “Well, we would never let you.”

And just like that, laughter fills the room, smashing Agatha’s nerves, wrapping her in warmth as she takes one trembling step closer toward the rest of her life.

—

Agatha’s hidden away in the main house, but she’s glued to the expansive window that allows her to see just down the path of trees to where their ceremony will be taking place. For the last thirty minutes, she’s watched colleagues, friends and mostly Rio’s family filter in and quickly be swept away in awe of the place. 

Agatha and Rio had laid the blueprint, but Wanda and Jen had brought it to life in a way she could’ve never imagined. 

The path down to the altar is brightened by the twinkle of candles floating atop water in glass vases placed intentionally on the ground, each one staggering in height. There’s lights stringing across the branches of the massive tree shading the mismatched wooden seats of their guests. It’s nearly sunset and everything looks soft and inviting just like each of them had wanted. 

They are fifteen minutes away from seeing each other, but Agatha swears it’s been fifteen minutes five times already. She’s pacing back and forth on the hardwood floor, her heels echoing around the room as she moves. It’s been a constant five minutes of her clacking before someone comes to check on her and it’s not anyone she would’ve thought.

It’s Benny and Matt. She freezes. “You two aren’t supposed to see me.”

Regardless, they both trek over to her, their hands in their pockets and suit jackets undone. Their relaxed posture only helps her but so much. She does find herself finally taking a deep breath

“Well, I cannot see you,” Matt chuckles, taking a seat on the couch in the middle of the room and beckoning her to sit next to him. 

“And I go where he goes,” Benny comments as he follows suit, sitting on the opposite side of the couch to the other man. 

Agatha sighs, but she does sit down and immediately fold into the couch. 

“What’s wrong,” Matt asks softly, his body turning towards her.

“Why does everyone think something is wrong,” Agatha gripes, her body falling back against the cushions as she looks up into the ceiling. 

“Okay, I’m sorry for assuming, but you’re not exactly selling your case right now.” 

Agatha lets out a dry chuckle. “I’m a little nervous. I don’t know why.”

Benny reaches forward and places a reassuring hand on her thigh, squeezing lightly. “You’re nervous because you care. I was the same way.”

“Well this sucks,” she laughs . They guys chuckles trickle in softly. “Normal girls have their dads here but mine and to be a deadbeat and go and die.”

Matt and Benny sit in silence for a second, unsure of their next move, but Agatha just waves them off. “You can laugh.”

The men just let out a dismissive breath, Matt speaking next. “Look, you may not have a dad here with you, but I know The Agatha Harkness is not scared of her moment to shine. What’s gotten into you?”

The older woman laughs, her head shaking softly. “Nobody said anything about being scared…”

Benny cuts in for a moment. “It’s okay if you are. I would be if I had all eyes on me while walking down the aisle in heels. I’d probably break an ankle—”

“Thank you, Benny,” Matt interrupts with a clearing of his throat. “What if…”

He pauses for a moment and looks over to Benny as if asking for his support. Agatha furrows her brow, looking between the two of them, ready to ask what is going on and then Benny is finishing for the two of them, “What if we walk you to Rio?”

The suggestion catches her off guard, her mouth snapping closed before opening again slowly. “You’d do that?”

Matt’s smile is soft, but sure. “In a heartbeat.”

Benny grins, a little brighter, trying to ease the heaviness. “Besides, we're going to be officially family in about thirty minutes anyways. I can hand you off to my sister happily.” 

Agatha laughs, watery but real, and the tension in her shoulders begins to ease. She looks between them with their steady presence, the easy affection in their eyes and something in her settles.

“I’d like that,” she whispers. 

Matt stands from the couch and extends his arm without hesitation, Benny mirroring on the other side. 

“Then it’s settled,” Matt says. “We’ll walk you to her.”

Agatha slips her hands through theirs, feeling steadied by the weight of them at either side. Her heart still pounds, but this time, it’s not just nerves. It’s anticipation, and love, and the deep comfort of not having to do it alone.

“Wanda’s going to kill us for going off script,” Agatha mutters between them, breaking the tension and sending a round of giggles through all of them as they make their way through the doors leading down to the start of the rest of Agatha’s life. 

The music swells, soft and deliberate. The signal that everything is beginning. Agatha’s pulse jumps, but Matt’s arm is steady beneath her hand, Benny’s presence warm at her other side. They exchange a silent look, before both lean down just slightly, speaking low enough only she can hear.

“You’ve got this,” Matt murmurs.

“And if you don’t,” Benny adds with a grin, “we’ve got you.”

Agatha laughs, breath catching, but the sound steadies her. They turn the corner of the forest where the guests await, all standing up on their feet. Their eyes are all following her in awe and she’s never been more grateful for Matt and Benny than in this moment. As they round to the start of the aisle, a rush of light and color greets her, but all of it blurs, fades, until her gaze finds Rio waiting at the far end.

Rio’s eyes shine the moment they meet hers, and her lips curve in that way that always makes Agatha feel like the rest of the world is a mere backdrop. The nerves that threatened to topple her just moments ago melt, replaced by a swell of certainty so strong it nearly buckles her knees.

Matt feels the shift in her posture and gives her arm a gentle squeeze. Benny leans in, whispering with a smirk, “There she is.”

Step by step, they carry her forward together, steadying her when her breath catches, grounding her as the aisle stretches before her. Every footstep brings her closer to Rio, closer to the life waiting at the end of that walk.

By the time they reach the altar, Agatha’s hand is trembling, but not from fear, from joy. Benny and Matt pause, each of them looking at her one last time before they let her go.

“Ready?” Matt asks quietly.

Agatha nods, eyes shimmering as they fix on Rio. “More than ready.”

Together, they place her hands gently into Rio’s, their smiles proud, eyes bright. Then they step back, leaving her exactly where she belongs.

And in that moment, the whole world falls away until it’s just Agatha and Rio, standing at the threshold of forever.

“God you look so beautiful, Agatha,” Rio whispers as she takes her eyes over every single fiber of the dress, the heels and Agatha’s freshly done nails. Rio’s hands are firm and grounding, but not as steadying as the look in the younger woman’s eyes as she blinks back the tears that are threatening to break free. Agatha abandoned the idea of holding hers back right after seeing Rio as she knew there was no point. Her tears flow freely down her face, but Rio’s quick to raise her thumb and brush them away lightly. 

The touch melts Agatha’s resolve. She feels herself relax into the sentiment and though the officiant has been talking this whole time, she hasn’t heard a word. Nothing else matters besides this woman and the love she has for her. Besides, Rio won’t let her slip. She’ll keep them both steady as they go through the ceremony together. 

And that she does. Rio holds her firm as she declares her love for Agatha loudly and proudly for all of their loved ones to hear. She keeps her eyes locked onto Agatha’s like a lifeline. The older woman continues rubbing the back of her hand with a soothing thumb as she urges her soon-to-be wife one—Rio doing the same. And when Rio slips the wedding band into her finger, everything around them crumbles and falls into place all at once. 

“I love you,” Rio whispers as she does so. 

“I love you more,” Agatha whispers back and then she slides the wedding band onto Rio’s finger, eyes brimming with tears and the promise of forever. 

And then the words, you may now kiss your bride, are spoken and they collide into one another like magnets that have even kept apart too long. Agatha’s hands grab Rio’s face, pulling her close as the younger woman wraps her hands around her wife’s waist, keeping her tight. There’s one long, steady kiss that turns into a few longer pecks before they break apart with smiles blistering each of their faces. 

“We did it,” Rio whispers against her lips.

“Fuck yeah we did,” Agatha whispers back with a giggle. 

They walk down the aisle hand in hand, ambushed with cheers from their guests filled with love. When they reach the end of the aisle, Rio makes a quick move to pull Agatha into her arms and over her shoulder as she runs them both back to the house, eager to steal a moment with her wife as the reception gets prepared for them. 

“Where are we even going,” Agatha huffs, grinning as Rio drops her back steadily onto her own two feet at the helm of the steps to the house.

“Anywhere we can be alone,” Rio fires back, eyes gleaming as she pulls her wife up the stairs, opening the door with purpose and ushering them inside. 

The door clicks shut behind them, and in an instant, Rio has Agatha pressed against it with her hands greedily clawing at her waist. Their mouths crash together, the kiss all heat and relief, as if the entire ceremony had only been a prelude to this.

“You’re my wife,” Rio breathes against her lips, the word tasting new and intoxicating.

Agatha shudders, her laugh breaking into a whimper as she drags Rio closer. “Say it again.”

“You’re my wife,” Rio whispers, this time lower, grazing the word against the curve of her throat.

“My wife,” Agatha insists as she fists the fabric of Rio’s shirt, pulling her impossibly close. She’s breathless and undone, feeling herself come apart as Rio puts her back together with purpose. Every kiss intentional. Every graze of her fingers lasting. They only pause for a moment as if to let the tension between them settle into something deeper.  

Rio’s hands roam without restraint, memorizing every line and fold of the gown, every shiver she draws out of Agatha she tucks for safe keeping. “Fuck, this dress was made is for you. You’re stunning.”

Agatha tips her head back against the door, laughter and desire tangling in her voice. Her nails graze the back of Rio’s neck, and the shiver that rips through her wife makes her grin. “All of it is yours, my love. I’m your wife now.”

The word becomes a prayer between them, traded back and forth between kisses, breaths, each repetition pulling them deeper into something untethered. Neither can stop themselves from smiling, even as the kisses grow hotter, more insistent, their joy spilling into every brush of lips and every gasp against the other’s mouth.

Rio’s hands slide along the silk of Agatha’s gown, restless, searching, until they find her waist and press her firmly against the door once more. Their mouths meet again in a kiss so consuming it leaves Agatha dizzy. Her knees feel weak. Her arms around Rio’s neck is the only thing holding her steady to this moment. 

Agatha gasps between kisses, the sound dissolving into a deep groan. “If we don’t stop, my dress won’t survive the night.”

Rio’s grin is wicked, her lips dragging down the column of Agatha’s throat as she sucks against it, definitely leaving marks in her wake. “Maybe that’s the point. If you weren’t so pretty right now, I’d tear it off of you without a second thought.”

The moan that rips through Agatha’s chest has her arching her back from the door, hips jutting against her wife’s desperately. It takes her a moment, but she strings together a coherent sentence that stops Rio in her tracks. “Yes, but then I'd be flashing the guests with what’s hiding underneath…”

“Agatha,” Rio says—a warning. She shudders, groaning low, her body taut like a bowstring. “If you keep talking like that, I’ll will tear off that dress and take you against this door.”

Agatha groans. “Baby, have you heard of bunching the dress around my waist? You don’t have to ruin it just yet.”

“Are you giving me permission to have a little taste,” Rio raises a brow. Her body starting to move downward as she begins to fall to her knees in front of the other woman, but Agatha catches her halfway, pulling her back up. 

Rio sets her jaw. “You’re unbelievable.”

The older woman leans forward, her voice dropping lowly as she lets her lips caress against Rio’s ear. “Baby you haven’t seen unbelievable yet.”

And then she pulls back, a tight smirk on her kiss-swollen lips as she sighs.“Besides, we should probably… not consummate the marriage against this door.”

Rio whimpers, cheeks flushed, tugging her wife back in for one last lingering, hungry kiss as if to savor it for the next few hours. When they part, Agatha’s smile is bright, even through her ragged breaths. Rio’s cheeks are pink, neck smeared with a lipstick stain that’s definitely not hers, but neither of them care to wipe away. Everyone knows who belongs to who here. It’s their day. 

“My wife,” Agatha murmurs between them once more, cupping the side of Rio’s face and kissing her quickly before they straighten themselves up.

Hand in hand, still grinning and flushed, they slip back toward the sound of the celebration, hearts thrumming in their chests with anticipation and excitement. 

“Ahh, there they are,” Wanda calls, lifting her glass high as soon as she sees them coming through the dark tree line. “Thought maybe we’d have to send a search party.”

They’re all sitting at the long table, lights strung above their heads and glasses definitely full of their second or third round of wine as a few waiters move in and out around them placing baskets of bread in between each few guests. There’s quiet conversations happening all throughout, everyone’s smiles lit by the candle light in front of them while the sound of music mixes in the air. 

Agatha’s chest feels full as Rio pulls her seat out for her and urges her to sit down and when she takes a seat next to her, they smile at one another, love drunk and happy. 

Jen smirks across from them, eyes flickering between the two of them. “Judging by those faces, I’d say we definitely shouldn’t have interrupted.”

Rio waves them off, placing an arm around Agatha proudly. “You can all tease us as much as you want because this is my wife and we can sneak off as much as we want to because this is our wedding..”

“This is going to be a thing all night, isn’t it,” Jen sighs.

“Let them have their moment, babe,” Alice hushes her wife, winking towards the two newlyweds. 

“For the record, I won the bet. I said they would sneak off before dinner and, well, here they are,” Jen adds, a raise with a celebratory raise of her glass. 

Matt clinks a glass with Jen’s from beside her. “Can we talk about the real issue here?”

Agatha looks at him. “Which is?”

“You two were gone for twenty three minutes and didn’t even bring back a sample of the food. Some of us are starving.”

“I’m sure food was far from their minds,”Alice snickers.

“Oh my god,” Benny groans from across the table from Matt and next to Rio.

“I’m not sorry I have a fast metabolism,” Matt argues while Karen slaps him lightly on the shoulder, cutting her eyes at him, but he just brushes her off with a smile. 

“You had three sliders and half a charcuterie board during cocktail hour,” Jen says incredulously.

“‘half’ is a little dramatic,” Matt says, unbothered. “The brie was just really good.”

Rio laughs, eyes lighting up as she presses a kiss to Agatha’s shoulder. “I missed you idiots.”

“We’re touched,” Benny says dryly as he bites into a roll, chewing harshly and drawing a snicker out of his sister.

A few moments pass, everyone filling themselves up on wine and bread as they wait for the first course of salads and soups to be passed around. No one is more excited than Matt, but Rio immediately notices the way he doesn’t touch his food at first, his mind seems occupied as he leans over to Karen and she nods softly to whatever he’d said. And then he stands, a knife clinking against his glass as everyone turns to him. 

“Alright,” he says. “I wasn’t going to do a real speech, but then Benny asked me to speak on both of our behalf and I didn’t want to disappoint him any more than I already have.”

A few laughs ripple through the room. Matt exhales, softer now. He seems to relax, but Agatha looks to Rio and she’s already fighting back her fears, lip quivering softly. 

“I’ve known Rio for… what, seven years now? Which sounds impossible because I swear we haven’t aged a day.” He pauses. “Except emotionally. Emotionally we’ve gone through at least nine lifetimes.”

More laughter, but quieter now. It’s soft and earnest. The eyes of loved ones delving into a story that would only give them more reasons to love her wife and Agatha’s heart soars. 

“When I met Rio, she was this tiny, stubborn ball of conviction and bad decisions. And I say that with love. She had no filter, no fear, and no concept of patience. But she also had this terrifying heart. The kind of heart that refuses to quit, or break, or, god, let anyone she cares about feel alone. She has saved my life more times than she knows.”

He swallows, looks down, composes himself, but his emotion wells thick with emotion. Rio’s crying fully now, the tears dripping off of her chin and Agatha just holds her hand tightly, leaning over to place a kiss on her shoulder as she leans her chin against it. 

“But I watched her go through years of pretending she didn’t need anything back. She took care of everybody else, defended everyone else, held all of us together… but she never believed she’d find someone strong enough to carry her too. To meet her at her level. To choose her on the loud days and the quiet ones.”

He looks at Agatha now.

“And then she met you.”

He laughs a little, far too emotional for Agatha to handle, but she catches every word he directs at her. “God, I hated you at first.”

The crowd laughs again, but Agatha just shakes her head fondly

“Not personally,” he adds quickly. “I just thought you were like every other CEO I knew. Too put together. Too controlling. Too… above it all. And then I realized, you were just someone who had already survived your own storms. Someone who didn’t flinch at chaos because you’d learned how to build a life in it. You didn’t tame Rio. You matched her. You challenged her. And you loved her without ever asking her to be smaller. And that… that’s everything.”

He looks between them, voice steady now but warm.

“People say soulmates are about fate. But I think they’re about choice. About choosing each other over and over again through every fight and every day that it would be easier to walk away. Rio and Agatha, I have never seen two people choose each other as hard or as fiercely as you do. And I’m proud to stand here and watch you build this life. Because if anyone deserves a forever that is loud and brave and stupid and beautiful, it’s you two.”

He lifts his glass.

“To Rio and Agatha, may your love stay wild and may your life together be your greatest adventure… and of course, enjoy. I love you both.”

There’s hardly a dry eye. Everyone is sniffling, wiping their eyes and noses as the subtle sound of glasses clinking mixes in. Rio and Agatha sit with their mouths agape, hearts full and tears shed. Never in a million years could Agatha have expected that emotional display from the man who’s been Rio’s steady rock for so long, but by god did he do it. And by the look on her wife’s face, she’s thinking the exact same thing. 

“Go hug him,” Agatha whispers against her temple softly as she watches her wife stand from her chair and quickly rush around the table and into the man’s arms. He doesn’t see her coming, but he catches her with grace, holding her tightly. 

Agatha wants to take her phone out and capture the moment forever, but she doesn’t. She holds onto the mental picture and keeps it tucked away. One day, she’ll look back on this memory and know it was for her alone to see and that alone is enough. 

Rio comes back to sit down, but not without surging down and kissing Agatha softly, her hand cupping against Agatha’s cheek and pulling her close. She tastes like wine and tears, but it’s the sweetest thing Agatha’s ever tasted. When they part, their foreheads are together and she’s smiling earnestly as she whispers between them, “Dance with me?”

Rio leans back and offers her hand to which Agatha takes without question. “Glady.” 

The younger woman pulls her to the carpeted dance floor under the low branches hanging with spanish moss and string lights, a cascade of candles littered around them. The soft melody of “I only have eyes for you,” by the flamingos starts to play and Agatha already feels the emotion welling in her throat.

Rio just holds her close, one wrapped around her waist and she sways them both to the beat slowly. Agatha just keeps on arms around her neck, scratching against the small hairs there absentmindedly as the older holds Rio’s firmly, hands clasped together between them. 

Rio looks down at their joined hands, the ring on Agatha’s finger now adorned with the wedding band, and she smiles. “I can’t believe you’re my wife.”

Agatha leans down and kisses her knuckles. “Believe it.” 

The younger woman just shakes her head, more so to shake away the tears and not to discredit her wife’s reassurance. “I always knew it. Deep down.”

Agatha raises an eyebrow, a smirk on her lips. “Is that so?”

“I believe I once told you I manifested you with candles,” Rio jokes, though Agatha briefly wonders if her wife has some truth lingering there. She doesn’t let her fester on it for long. “I came into your office with a purpose. I wanted you. I didn’t care how I made it happen. I was going to make you remember me. Make you want me.”

This is news to Agatha. She’d never bothered to ask why Rio had been so brazen during her interview, only just passing it off as her personality or some sick death wish. But never anything more than that. “You never told me that.”

“I never thought about it,” the lawyer shrugs it off.

Agatha looks at her incredulously. “So you knew I had a fiance and that you’d be my intern for three months, but still kept pursuing.”

Rio nods. “Yes. And I do it all again. Even if you didn’t choose me in the end. I’d still go back to those three months and do everything over.”

Agatha’s hand squeezes Rio’s hard as if anchoring herself to the reality of it. “You really would do it all over? Even knowing how messy it would be?”

Rio laughs softly, that deep, easy sound that always makes Agatha’s knees weak and the older woman falls into it like she does every single time. “Every moment. Every fight, every sleepless night, every time I almost drove you crazy… Even Ralph attacking me. I’d do it all. Because it led to this. To you.”

Agatha swallows, her chest tight with the weight of confession and desire. “I—” she starts, then pauses, unable to articulate the whirlwind inside her. Instead, she leans in, pressing her forehead against Rio’s. “I’m so glad you did.”

Rio smiles against her temple. “Good. Because I’m not letting you go. Not ever.”

And in that quiet, charged moment, all the chaos of their past falls away, leaving only the certainty of each other. Agatha holds her tighter, the tears burning her eyes, but it lacks in comparison to the way her love burns for Rio. The younger woman just sways them softly until the song comes to a close, kissing Agatha soundly as the final chords sound and the cheers of their friends and family take over. When they both part and look to them, Agatha’s surprised to find her friends crying, Wanda being the most inconsolable to no surprise. 

Rio pulls her softly back to the table, keeping their hands clasped between them resting atop the surface as they eat and chat with their friends, pretending that they aren’t burning to leave and actually consummate this for real this time But despite it, they stay calm and enjoy the love surrounding them. 

Somewhere in the mix of it all, the table starts to dwindle low with guests arranging their exits and giving their best wishes to the newlyweds, but of course, the core stays. They stay seated at the table, a bottle of wine passing around between them as they take on a much more relaxed posture. Those in suits have loosened their ties, unbuttoned their collars and removed their jackets. Sleeves are rolled up and heels are removed. 

Somehow, a bottle of whiskey has found its way into the mix and Agatha has lost track of how many shots they’ve taken, but she feels alright. 

“Rio was literally obsessed with Agatha,” Matt nearly slurs, his glass sloshing about in his hand as Karen leans against his arm to steady it.

“I was not,” Rio exclaims, appalled. 

“She so was,” Matt confirms, pointing an accusing finger his best friend’s way. “She was the one who told me about the internship. She literally was ready to do whatever it took to get it. I remember her yearning. It was disgusting. She wouldn’t shut up about your hair—”

“Okay, thank you,” Rio cuts in, her cheeks flushed but Agatha’s just curled into her neck giggling, placing soft kisses into her warm skin. 

“Darling, we’re married. It’s okay if you’re obsessed with me,” Agatha affirms, but Rio just blows a rift of air against her forehead. 

“Besides, we all knew it, Rio,” Jen comments, earning a groan of approval from Benny whose head is laying against the cool surface of the table. 

“How come you all always tell me how obsessed with her I am,” Rio cries, eyes cutting to each of her friends. “You never say Agatha is obsessed with me! She literally ended her relationship of twenty years for me!”

“Hey,” the older woman yelps, smacking Rio softly on her arm.

“It’s true, Agatha,” Jen agrees, narrowly dodging the roll that was quickly thrown her way. 

“All of you shut up,” Agatha warns, but she’s laughing and smiling at each of them. “Why don’t we talk about how Rio flirted with Wanda to get into my office?”

There’s a series of what’s from the group, all of them looking back and forth between Rio and the redhead who’s girlfriend is firmly staring daggers at her.

“It was not like that,” Wanda cries, looking to Rio for help to which the raven haired girl quickly offers. 

“Agatha is dramatic and jealous. It’s hardly like she’s making it sound.”

“So make it sound better,” Nat says with a teasing lilt, though Agatha notices the jealousy seeping through her tone. She watches as Wanda wraps an arm around her and tugs her close, but the blonde doesn’t so much as budge. 

“I told her that her hair looks nice so that she would let me into Agatha’s office. I wanted to give her a coffee so that she would fuck me,” Rio dead pans, a smirk on her lips as Agatha gasps beside her, smacking her wide yet again.

“I’m not that easy,” the CEO exclaims, but Jen just clears her throat from across the table. Agatha holds her hand up immediately. “Don’t you start.”

“I didn’t say anything.”

“You didn’t have to.”

“Sounds like there’s a story there,” Rio urges teasingly, but neither woman bites. 

“Speaking of easy,” Wanda changes the subject, eager to get Nat’s dark eyes off of her. “Who gave it up first?”

“What?!”

It’s hard to decipher who’s shock was the loudest, but Agatha knows for certain hers gave everyone a run for their money.

“There’s no way she just asked that,” Alice says in disbelief. “She’s the last person to talk about kissing let alone sex.”

“Well, I’m curious,” she says, no doubt tipsy.

Agatha hadn’t planned on answering, but Rio seems to have had different plans. “Agatha fucked me first.”

“I knew it,” Matt shrieks to everyone’s surprise just as Benny starts groaning and covering his ears. His wife just laughs next to him, watching him suffer. “Rio was way too happy and, Agatha, you were still, well, brooding.”

“I’m shocked,” Alice says softly, but her wife just shushes her. 

“I’m not. Agatha was wild in college. I told her once I wouldn’t be surprised if she had fifty children existing purely out of spite.” 

“Fifty,” Rio says, her voice pitched a little too high to pass off as anything but what it is, jealously. 

“Yes, fifty,” Jen confirms. “She had a revolving door of wom—”

“That’s enough, Jen,” Agatha shushes her again, ignoring the way Rio seems to tighten next to her for her own well being.

“So, Agatha was gay before Rio,” Wanda asks softly, eyes jumping between her former boss and her best friend across the table. The older woman ignores the way she wants to correct Wanda for the sake of time and her sanity. 

“Yes, it’s a long story, but one that we don’t have time to tell tonight unfortunately,” Agatha waves it off, downing the rest of the wine in her glass as she abruptly stands from the table, catching all of her friends off guard. “Does anyone fancy a swim?”

“Yes, let’s bring all the drunk people to the ocean, Agatha,” Jen rolls her eyes.

“Damn it. You spoiled my plan for my mass sacrifice,” Agatha says sarcastically, waving off her best friend and looking down to her wife with an offered hand. “Join me?”

Rio eyes her cautiously. “Are you sure you don’t want one of your fifty other baby mama’s to go with you?”

Agatha sighs, looking at Jen with tight eyes. “See what you do?” 

“I believe it is what you did Agatha.”

“Guys,” Alice cuts in. “Let’s just fucking go swimming.” 

“Horray,” Benny chirps as he quickly pulls his head from the table, nearly toppling over his wife in the process, but they eventually just melt into giggles. “Last one to the ocean is a shrimp!”

“Shrimp,” Matt asks in a whisper-yells, but everyone just brushes Benny off and makes way down the sandy path behind the trees. Rio goes to follow, but Agatha pulls her back softly by their joined hands.

“What,” Rio says flatly, her brows narrowing. 

“There are no fifty baby mama’s or fifty children,” Agatha says softly, her eyes searching between Rio’s very glossy browns. “The only person I want to have a child with is you.”

The younger woman’s eyes widen, her mouth slightly agape. “You’re serious?”

“Yes,” Agatha says firmly. “Though we’ll need to be sober when we talk about this and there’s a lot more involved, obviously, but it doesn’t make it any less true. I want you to be the mother to my children. No one else.”

Rio seems to sparkle at this, her smile widening as she surges forward and picks Agatha off of the ground, swinging them around in circles as the happiness radiates off of them in droves. Agatha’s giggling like she’s twenty and no time has passed while Rio keeps her held tightly, eventually sliding Agatha down into her arms and keeping her pressed into her front. 

“I love you, Agatha Harkness,” Rio says softly, tears brimming. “I can’t wait for this life with you.” 

Agatha isn’t sure how she got so lucky. She’d spent what felt like a lifetime empty, roaming around without a purpose and now she’s got a life she could’ve never imagined, but yearned for regardless. There’s a group of friends turned family that she can’t see herself living without. They turn her inside out and upside down by pulling every last nerve in her body, but her life is never boring, her days are never short and her life will never drag on.

And then there’s Rio. The magnetic burst of energy that she is all wrapped into the beautiful body, mind and soul of a twenty seven year old that Agatha could’ve never seen coming. She’s not sure who she was before Rio, but she doesn’t find she misses whoever it was. Rio has made her better, kept her stronger and wills her to be the best version of herself. She’d follow her anywhere.

And as she follows her down to the beach, their giggles tangling in the salty night air as the sand kicks up between their feet, she looks at her. Really looks at her, and sees the rest of her life unfold between her eyes and she’s never been happier.
